Daqri

âš°ï¸ 2019
Daqri was an augmented reality hardware startup that specialized in creating integrated AR solutions for industrial applications. Their flagship product was the Daqri Smart Helmet, designed to overlay digital information on a real-world view to enhance worker productivity and safety. Targeting industries such as construction and manufacturing, the helmet offered heads-up display features for maneuvering complex workspaces, executing precise tasks, and accessing instructional content seamlessly. Despite raising substantial investment, Daqri struggled with market adoption, hardware challenges, and competition, ultimately leading to its asset liquidation in 2019, with Snap acquiring most of the assets.

The service was offered as a perk to hotel guests, making the travel experience seamlessly connected and informed.

Glitch

âš°ï¸ 2012
Glitch, developed by Tiny Speck before the transition to Slack, was a massively multiplayer online game that encouraged player creativity and community interaction through a vibrant, surreal environment. Co-founded by Stewart Butterfield, the game was ahead of its time, focusing on world-building and user-generated content, but its financial model couldn't sustain its operational needs, particularly in a landscape not yet conducive to monetizing such interactions. Glitch paved the way for Slack's communication tools by marrying social networking with collaborative gameplay.

FoundationDB

âš°ï¸ 2015
FoundationDB was a cutting-edge, distributed NoSQL database system that boasted true ACID transactions and horizontal scalability. Designed to be a powerful solution for backend reliability, it competed directly with other NoSQL databases by focusing on speed and reduced hardware costs through its efficient architecture. A key feature of FoundationDB was its ability to allow developers to layer various models, offering unmatched flexibility in data schema design, a critical functionality for developers building complex applications. Its unique architecture enabled developers to handle advanced use-cases requiring robust data integrity while maintaining performance, which was a significant draw for enterprises dealing with large-scale data management.

The core idea was to integrate donations into the checkout process, allowing customers to contribute a percentage of their purchase to a selected charity, thereby increasing brand loyalty and conversion rates. GiveSpark's value proposition lay in its ability to create a feel-good factor for customers while offering brands a unique marketing angle to differentiate themselves in a crowded market.

Answer.ky

âš°ï¸ 2013
Answer.ky was an on-demand question and answer service aimed at providing users with instant responses to their queries. The platform connected users to a network of experts and enthusiasts who could provide detailed and knowledgeable answers in real-time. Its value proposition centered around the immediacy and reliability of information, leveraging a crowd-sourced model to ensure a wide range of expertise and perspectives.

Latergramme

âš°ï¸ 2017
Latergramme was an early pioneer in the social media scheduling space, primarily focused on Instagram. The company provided a platform that allowed users to schedule and manage their Instagram posts efficiently. This offered a significant advantage to social media managers and brands looking to maintain a consistent presence on Instagram without the hassle of manual posting. Latergramme's value proposition centered around saving time and optimizing content strategies by allowing users to plan and schedule posts in advance, thereby enhancing engagement and reach.

Ecomom

âš°ï¸ 2013
Ecomom was an ecommerce platform focusing on eco-friendly products for children and families. Founded in 2009, the startup aimed to capitalize on the rising trend of conscious consumerism, targeting parents who were increasingly concerned about the environmental and health impacts of the products they used for their children. The platform offered a curated selection of organic, non-toxic, and sustainable products ranging from baby food and diapers to toys and household items. It promised a convenient shopping experience with the added assurance of safety and sustainability, attempting to build trust with its target demographic by filtering products through rigorous ethical and environmental criteria. The unique value proposition of Ecomom lay in its promise to be more than just a retailer; it positioned itself as a community hub for eco-conscious parents. They provided educational resources, parenting tips, and a platform for like-minded parents to connect and share experiences. This model aimed to deepen customer loyalty and drive repeat purchases by embedding the brand into the daily lives of its users. However, despite its noble intentions and growing consumer interest in sustainable products, Ecomom struggled to scale its operations or achieve sustainable profitability.
